  1808. # [12:30] <mcsmurf> basically the idea behind hg queue is: You don't commit (permanently) anymore in the local repository (except when checking in something on the official mozilla-central repository)
  1809. # [12:30] * Quits: smooney (smooney@moz-A268C4E8.red-81-44-172.dynamicip.rima-tde.net) (Quit: smooney)
  1810. # [12:30] <mcsmurf> but you start with a command like "hg qnew bug_1234"
  1811. # [12:30] * Quits: Optimizer (Optimizer@27EBAA80.1163B72F.2AB48280.IP) (Ping timeout)
  1812. # [12:30] <mcsmurf> then you change the code and after that use the command "hg qrefresh"
  1813. # [12:31] <mcsmurf> then your changes have been saved in a file like the one that has been attached to the bug
  1814. # [12:31] <mcsmurf> and with "hg qpop" and "hg qpush"
  1815. # [12:31] <mcsmurf> you can always remove/add your change again
  1816. # [12:31] <mcsmurf> (qpop is remove, qpush is apply to the local repository)
  1817. # [12:32] <sudheera> hm interesting. thanks :) :)
  1818. # [12:32] * Joins: JeroenDeDauw1 (j@moz-BE92FD45.dip.t-dialin.net)
  1819. # [12:32] <mcsmurf> and you can also create multiple patches with another "hg qnew bla" command
  1820. # [12:32] * Joins: Standard8 (Standard8@B7F1AE36.48015583.54C3481B.IP)
  1821. # [12:32] * Quits: chrisccoulson (chr1s@moz-6A3A134E.cust-13020.ip.static.uno.uk.net) (Quit: Ex-Chat)
  1822. # [12:33] <mcsmurf> so you have a stack of patches (diff files) that you can always remove/add to the local repository
